## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. In chemical kinetics, rate laws typically express dA/dt as polynomial powers of concentration, with possible time-dependent forcing or catalytic effects.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order decay: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, first-order reactions)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction kinetics)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with constant product concentration)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, photochemistry)
- Parallel pathways with time: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A * t (time-modulated kinetics)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant source/sink)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill-type): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)
- Second-order with equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic rate law with source term)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) suggests a classical autonomous rate law; check if dA/dt = f(A) alone fits well before adding time dependence
- Integer power-law dependence on A (orders 0, 1, 2, 3) reflects molecularity of elementary reaction steps
- Rational functions of A (e.g., A/(c+A)) indicate enzyme-like saturation where a catalyst or binding site is limiting
- Product of A and (c-A) terms indicates autocatalytic or logistic behavior where both reactant and product concentrations matter
- Explicit time dependence in the rate law suggests external forcing (e.g., light intensity variation, temperature ramps) or integration of a multi-species system into a single-variable effective equation
- Negative sign of leading coefficient indicates consumption/decay of species A; positive indicates production or autocatalysis
- Square root dependence A**0.5 can arise from chain reaction mechanisms (e.g., radical kinetics with termination steps)
- Multiple additive terms in the rate law suggest parallel reaction pathways or competing mechanisms operating simultaneously
